<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">Carbon nanotube (CNT) composites are sensitive to the presence of gases due to their high surface-to-volume ratio and hollow structure that are well suited for gas molecule absorption and storage. Such sensing capability is here integrated with UHF RF identification (RFID) technology to achieve passive and low-cost sensors, remotely readable. CNT film (buckypaper) is used as a localized variable resistive load integrated into a tag antenna, which becomes able to transduce the presence of hazardous gas in the environment, ammonia in this case, into a change of its electromagnetic features. The dynamic range and the hysteresis of the radio sensor are investigated by simulations, equivalent circuits, and articulated experimentations within a true RFID link, providing the proof of concept and some guidelines for tag design.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Recently, there has been increasing effort toward combining the capabilities of sensors and wireless devices in order to collect, process, and transmit time-varying information about objects/personnel. RF identification (RFID) passive sensing has been successfully explored as a low-cost candidate toward lightweight, reliable, energy-efficient, and even batteryless durable wireless sensing devices. Proposed examples, already theoretically investigated or experimentally tested, include: temperature sensing <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, solar powered and piezo-scavenging batteryless wireless sensor tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, human monitoring by means of implanted devices <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, biochemical sensors <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, strain sensor <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, motion sensor <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, moisture <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, and gas detection <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>. However, there is still significant work to do to fully master the cohabitation and integration of sensing and communication capabilities <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>.</p><p>One of the most attractive applications of wireless sensors is the remote monitoring of environments to detect the presence of hazardous gases within industrial sites (supply chain and food integrity) or to control the quality of work spaces. Traditional gas-sensing mechanisms exploit vapor-sensitive polymers, semiconductor metal oxides, or porous structures as sensitive material, which require microfabrication techniques, power supply, and data-processing electronics that may preclude many low-cost monitoring applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. Carbon nanotube (CNT) composites <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> have been recently found to perform as a gas sensor due to their high surface-to-volume ratio and hollow structure that are well suited for gas molecules absorption and storage. Upon exposure to small quantities of certain gases, CNTs change their physical properties, such as their electrical conductance (molecules act as electron donors or acceptors), and this variation can be easily detected by various methods <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>. Concerning wireless systems, for example, a CNT-based inductor-capacitor resonant circuit (<i>LC</i>) with a multiwall CNT-SiO2 composite as a sensing layer has been proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a> as a passive wireless gas sensor. The presence of gas in the air produces a change of the dielectric properties of the CNT coating, and hence of the resonant frequency of the system, detectable by a loop antenna located approximately 15 cm from the sensor. However, the extremely low frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\sim {\hbox {10 MHz}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 MHz</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">(\sim {\hbox {10 MHz}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the magnetic coupling between the radiating structures make the proposed platform not suitable for medium/long-range applications. The same sensing approach has been evaluated also in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a> for a wired configuration.</p><p>From a different side, several CNT-based antennas have also been developed for their attractive characteristics. Due to the very high inductance per unit length <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a>, it is possible to fabricate CNT nanoantennas, while their relatively low cost, wide bandwidth, and simplicity of fabrication can indeed offer great advantages in RFID applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a>. Finally, the good mechanical properties of this kind of material, such as flexibility, strength, and low weight, suggests interesting opportunities in wearable electronics and antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a>.</p><p>While the idea to integrate sensing carbon nanostructures into a passive RFID tag was first introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, no attempt has been done up to date to design, fabricate, and test a complete CNT-tag working as a medium-range passive radio sensor.</p><p>In this context, this work is aimed to theoretically and experimentally demonstrate for the first time the feasibility of a fully working RFID sensor tag doped with single-wall carbon nanotubes (SWCNTs) sensitive to the presence of ammonia gas and to characterize its true sensing capabilities and limitations. The physical rationale of the proposed sensor lies in the clear dependence of the tag's radiation performances on the physical and chemical features of the integrated CNT, strongly affected by the close surrounding environment (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>). When the environment where the tag is placed undergoes changes in time, due to the presence of ammonia or other gases, the CNT's electrical features (mainly the conductivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) accordingly change. These variations affect the tag's performance and can be remotely detected by the reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Change of the electromagnetic response of RFID gas sensor can be related to a variation of the features of the integrated CNT, e.g., its conductivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-14" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\Delta\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>This paper is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> will be focused on the fabrication and characterization of the SWCNT <i>buckypaper</i>, to be used as part of the radio-sensor. The RFID sensing paradigm, as well as its basic equations, are then recalled in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> with particular attention to the definition of useful sensing identifiers, which can be easily extracted from raw measured data. The design of the RFID passive radio sensor is then discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> by means of equivalent circuit model and experimentations. Finally, in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>, the sensing features of the CNT-based RFID tag are fully investigated in the American and European UHF band by means of many experimental tests.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>SWCNT Material Preparation and Characterization</h2></div><p>Several deposition techniques have been proposed for CNT-based antennas and electronics: inkjet and screen-printing procedures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>, chemical vapor deposition (CVD) processes <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_2">[19]</a>, and thin films <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_2">[18]</a> are recent examples of useful techiques able to offer high conductive CNT samples.</p><p>SWCNT film, also referred to as buckypaper, offers isotropic conductivity, good mechanical strength and flexibility and gives the possibility to easily cut out the shape of the desired antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_2">[21]</a>. The fabrication procedure generally consists of filtering SWCNT suspension in acqueous or organic media, such as Triton X-100 or dimethyl formamide (DMF), under positive or negative pressure.</p><p>In this work, an alternative preparation method is presented, where the filtration over membrane has been replaced by evaporation in a controlled environment. The process is schematically shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. A 100-mg purified high functionality with carbonaceous purity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\geq</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-18" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">≥</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">\geq</script></tex-math></inline-formula>90% SWCNT powder from Carbon Solutions Inc., Riverside, CA, has been dispersed in 66 mL of water by sonication at 30 W for 60 min. Next, in order to get rid of the water and form the CNT buckypaper, the dispersion has undergone an overnight evaporation at 70 °C. Finally, a circular sheet with diameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d=90 {\hbox {mm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-21" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">90</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">d=90 {\hbox {mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has been produced over a polyamide membrane. The thickness of the buckypaper is determined by the total amount of CNTs used in the dispersion per unit surface of the membrane since the water is removed during the evaporation process. It can be evaluated in first approximation by a simple mathematical proportion with the density and thickness achieved in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_2">[22]</a>. With a calculated density <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S=1.6\times 10^{-2} {\hbox{mg}}/{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-31" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.6</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.96em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 1.024em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-40"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-42" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-44"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mg</span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-48"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-50" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-51"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-53"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-54"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-55"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-57"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-58"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">S=1.6\times 10^{-2} {\hbox{mg}}/{\hbox {mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the thickness results to be about 32 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-60" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-61"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-62" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-65"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-67"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-68" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Buckypaper preparation steps.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The sonication and the evaporation/filtration procedures are extremely critical for optimizing the CNT buckypaper performance. Large CNT agglomerates in the CNT solution will dominate leading to a brittle film, as well as a nonuniform evaporation produces a nonuniform sheet with holes, and consequently nonisotropic conductive performances. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the result of the process: the CNT buckypaper appears macroscopically uniform (a), but some undesired inconsistencies are present at the center of the sample (b) leading to poor and not uniform conductivity and mechanical properties.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>CNT buckypaper. (a) Prepared sample. (b) Irregularities of the sample toward the center. (c) CNT buckypaper monopole over the ground plane.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. RF Characterization</h3><p>The dielectric properties of the CNT are strictly dependent on their deposition techniques. Concentration, orientation, number of layers, and material type are important parameters that affect the performances of the nanotubes, especially at RF. Although several characterization data have been presented, especially in dc, the dielectric properties at RF are not univocally defined, making it necessary to preliminarily characterize the produced buckypaper. Here, an indirect method, using both measurements and computer simulations, has been used to refine the different values available in the literature according to our specific sample. Based on the assumption that the CNT can be considered a lossy metal (with finite conductivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-69" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-70"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-71" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), several strips of the CNT buckypaper of size 80 mm×5 mm were cut out of the membrane and plated on foam substrates in order to form monopole antennas in the RFID UHF frequency band. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(c)</a> shows a photograph of one of the monopole antennas used in the measurement setup. A silver epoxy mixture was applied at the interface CNT antenna—SMA connector and cured to improve their electrical and mechanical connectivity. The input impedance of the CNT antennas has been measured by means of a vector network analyzer (VNA) (Rohde&amp;Schwarz ZVA8). In parallel, finite-difference time-domain (FDTD) simulations were performed by varying the unknown <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-72" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> around the value available in literature. The CNT layer was accounted by a surface impedance model. A root mean square (rms) minimization has been finally applied in order to fit the measured and simulated input impedances and thus evaluate the conductivity. The optimum value obtained for the buckypaper after averaging on different monopole geometries was <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma\approx 2.5 {\hbox{S}}/{\hbox{m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-75" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-76"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-77" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≈</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.5</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-80"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-81"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-82"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-83"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-84" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-85"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-86"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-87" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-88"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-89"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-92" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">\sigma\approx 2.5 {\hbox{S}}/{\hbox{m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Sensing Characterization</h3><p>The response of the CNT to the ammonia is investigated here by analyzing the variation of the radiation performances of one of the previous monopoles (size 80 mm×5 mm) in term of both input impedance and transmission characteristics.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec2b1"><h4>1. Input Impedance</h4><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> (thick line) shows the measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-93" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-94"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-95"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-96" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-97"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-98"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">Z_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the CNT antenna before the exposure to ammonia. The monopole is strongly capacitive with a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-110\leq jX_{\rm in}\leq-70 \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-101" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; <p></p><p>A volume of 6 mL of commercial off-the-shelf 10% ammonia hydroxide was then guided into the 460-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox {cm}}^{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-205" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-206"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-207"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.26em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-208"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-209"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-210"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-211"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-212" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">cm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.264em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-213"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-214"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-215" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">{\hbox {cm}}^{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> plastic chamber surrounding the monopole. Upon the addition of the ammonia, a quick and strong variation of the monopole impedance was recorded. This is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-216" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-218"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-219" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-220"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-221"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-222" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">t_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> implies the time the measurements were recorded right after the introduction of the gas. The effect is monotonic for both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{R}_{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-223" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-224"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-225"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-226"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-227"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-228" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-229"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-230"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-231" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-232" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">{R}_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{X}_{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-233" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-234"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-235"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.84em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-236"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-237"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-238" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">X<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-239"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-240"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-241" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-242" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">{X}_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> during the whole exposure <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t_{4}-t_{1}\approx 15 {\hbox{min}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-243" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-244"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-245"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-246" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-247"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-248"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">4</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-250" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-252" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-253"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-254"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-255" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-256" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≈</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-257" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">15</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-259"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-260"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-261"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-262" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">min</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">t_{4}-t_{1}\approx 15 {\hbox{min}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As time progresses, slight saturation in the recorded measurements is observed.</p><p>The recovery of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Z}_{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-263" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-264"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-265"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-266"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-267"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-268" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-269"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-270"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-272" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">{Z}_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to its initial value was monitored after removing the ammonia from the chamber (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>). As in the exposure process, the variation is monotonic, but much slower (here, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t_{3}-t_{1}\approx 1 {\hbox{h}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-273" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-274"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-276" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-277"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-278"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-279" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-280" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-281" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-283"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-284"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-285" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-286" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≈</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-287" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-288"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-289"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-291"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-292" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">t_{3}-t_{1}\approx 1 {\hbox{h}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). A slight difference between the input impedances before the exposure to ammonia and after the recovery phase is observed as well, demonstrating the quite irreversible effect of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-293" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-294"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-295"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.5em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-296"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-298"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-300" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">NH</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 1.505em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-301"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-303" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the CNT. This effect is well known in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2b1">[15]</a>, and it is caused by the nature of gas absorption and desorption process to the nanotubes.

<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b2"><h4>2. Transmission</h4><p>Two identical CNT monopoles fabricated as before are now faced and separated by 20 cm to measure the transmission characteristics or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S_{21}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-354" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-355"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-356"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-357" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-358"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-359"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-360" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">S_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with and without <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-361" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-362"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-363"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.5em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-364"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-365"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-366"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-367"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-368" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">NH</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 1.505em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-369"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-371" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This measurement gives an evaluation of the variation of the gain in the presence of gas, which is proportional to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert S_{12}\vert^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-372" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-373"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-374" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-375"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-376" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-377"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-378"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-379" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">12</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-380"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.18em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-381" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.303em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-382"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-383"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-384" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">\vert S_{12}\vert^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between the two antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_2b2">[23]</a>. Only one monopole is exposed to the ammonia, according to the setup previously described. The measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S_{21}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-385" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">S_{21}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> upon adding <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-392" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; The measurement times are defined similarly to those of <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2b1" class="fulltext-link">Section II-B.1</a> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t_{4}-t_{1}\approx 15 {\hbox{min}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-403" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-407"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-408"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-409" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-414"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-415" style="font-size: 70.7%; position: relative; width: 1.921em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1001.46em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-453"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-454"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-455"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-456"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-457" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">NH</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; <p></p><p>Without ammonia (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> thick line), <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S_{12}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-461" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-462"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-463"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-464" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-465"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-466"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-467" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">12</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">S_{12}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has an average value of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim-{\hbox{40}} {\hbox {dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-468" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-469"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-470" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∼</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-471" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-472"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-473"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-475"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-476" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">40</span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-477"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-478"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-479"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-480"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-481" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">\sim-{\hbox{40}} {\hbox {dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the UHF band, suggesting the low conductivity of the radiating structures. Similarly to the input impedance, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S_{12}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-482" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-483"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-484"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-485" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-486"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-487"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-488" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">12</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">S_{12}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> changes monotonically in the presence of gas as time progresses. It is observed that a quick response takes place upon the addition of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-489" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-490"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-491"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.5em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-492"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-493"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-494"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-495"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-496" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">NH</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 1.505em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-497"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-499" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as well as saturation phenomena as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t\rightarrow t_{4}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-500" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-502" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">→</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.246em 1000.3em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-505" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-506"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-507"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-508" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">4</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">t\rightarrow t_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The transmission performance deteriorates as the antenna is exposed to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-509" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.5em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-512"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-513"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-514"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-515"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-516" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">NH</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 1.505em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-518"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, losing almost 7 dB. This effect seems to confirm a decrease in conductivity, as experienced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2b2">[10]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2b2">[15]</a>. This can be explained considering that this gas is a reducing agent that injects electrons to the nanotubes (p-type) reducing the number of holes, and hence, the conductivity.</p><p>Recovery features are still present, but slower than in the previous experiment. The permanent effects of the gas are clearly visible: the recovery variation is about 4 dB, almost half of the one achieved during the exposure process.</p><p>From these experiments, it is hence clear that the presence of ammonia affects both the impedance and gain of the monopole, potentially promising interesting applications in the RFID domain.</p></div></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>RFID-Sensing Equations</h2></div><p>It is assumed to denote with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Psi (t)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-520" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-521"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-522" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ψ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-523" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-524" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-525" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">\Psi (t)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> the concentration of ammonia in the air that has to be detected by the RFID platform.</p><p>The well-known <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_3">[24]</a> two-way reader-tag link may be rewritten, making explicit the dependence on the variation of local parameters with the purpose to obtain some sensing indicators, which can be directly derived by the reader's measurements <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a>. ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1-2" href="#deqn1-2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> and collected by it are <disp-formula id="deqn1-2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">P_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> through the reader's antenna forcing the tag to respond. It can be derived from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1-2" href="#deqn1-2" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> as follows, considering <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\rightarrow T}=P_{\rm{chip}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">P_{R\rightarrow T}=P_{\rm{chip}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that is the microchip sensitivity: <disp-formula id="deqn5" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P^{\rm to}[\Psi]=\left({{\lambda_{0}}\over{4\pi d}}\right)^{-2}{{P_{\rm{chip}}}\over{G_{R}(\theta,\phi)\eta_{p}G_{T}[\theta,\phi,\Psi]\tau\left[\Psi\right]}}.\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex;
