mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-68">G_{\tau}[\Psi]=\left({{4\pi d}\over{\lambda_{o}}}\right){{P_{\rm{chip}}}\over{G_{R}(\theta_{R},\phi_{R})P^{\rm to}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">G_{\tau}[\Psi]=\left({{4\pi d}\over{\lambda_{o}}}\right){{P_{\rm{chip}}}\over{G_{R}(\theta_{R},\phi_{R})P^{\rm to}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>Finally, forward <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1-2" href="#deqn1-2" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> and backward <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1-2" href="#deqn1-2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> powers may be combined at turn-on with the purpose to drop out the influence of the distance and of the reader and tag gains and orientation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_3">[26]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_3">[27]</a>. A nondimensional indicator, denoted as an analog identifier (AID), can hence be introduced <disp-formula id="deqn7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]=&amp;\,{{P_{\rm{chip}}}\over{2\sqrt{P_{R\leftarrow T}[\Psi]P_{}^{\rm to}[\Psi]}}}= R_{\rm{chip}}\left\vert Z_{\rm{chip}}+Z_{A}\left[\Psi\right]\right\vert^{-1}\cr&amp;&amp;{\hbox{(7)}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-69">\eqalignno{{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]=&amp;\,{{P_{\rm{chip}}}\over{2\sqrt{P_{R\leftarrow T}[\Psi]P_{}^{\rm to}[\Psi]}}}= R_{\rm{chip}}\left\vert Z_{\rm{chip}}+Z_{A}\left[\Psi\right]\right\vert^{-1}\cr&amp;&amp;{\hbox{(7)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]=&amp;\,{{P_{\rm{chip}}}\over{2\sqrt{P_{R\leftarrow T}[\Psi]P_{}^{\rm to}[\Psi]}}}= R_{\rm{chip}}\left\vert Z_{\rm{chip}}+Z_{A}\left[\Psi\right]\right\vert^{-1}\cr&amp;&amp;{\hbox{(7)}}}</span></span></disp-formula> and it is very useful when the interrogation setup changes (position and orientation) in successive measurements. The AID, in fact, just depends on the impedance mismatch and is immune to the interrogation modalities.</p><p>The two indicators in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> may be used as <i>data inversion curves</i> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">p[\Psi(t)]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">p[\Psi(t)]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between the measured data and the evolution <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Psi(t)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">\Psi(t)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the process. They are independent since the tag undergoes change in gain and impedance mismatch.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>RFID Gas Sensor: Design and Prototype</h2></div><p>There are several options to achieve a gas-sensitive tag taking advantage of the sensing feature of the CNT demonstrated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>. A first classification could be done considering the CNT as a part of the antenna radiating structure, e.g., an antenna totally or partially made of nanotubes, or considering instead the buckypaper as a doping component of the tag, e.g., a variable load properly placed in close proximity of the radiating elements <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_4">[10]</a>. Both solutions offer advantages and drawbacks; the best tradeoff between communication and sensing must be finally adopted. By considering the CNT as a radiating element, it is possible to maximize the gas sensitivity of the device; however, lowering the antenna efficiency and the activation distance of the RFID tag. These two parameters, together with the cost, are essential in RFID systems. The other solution, on the contrary, offers better communication and cost performances, but could provide a weaker sensitivity to the gas.</p><p>In this work, CNT film is used as a loading impedance of a conventional RFID passive tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_4">[10]</a>. The considered antenna layout is a copper dipole with an inductively coupled loop <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4">[28]</a>, matched to an NXP IC with complex impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm{chip}}=16-j148 \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">Z_{\rm{chip}}=16-j148 \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and sensitivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm{chip}}=-15 {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">P_{\rm{chip}}=-15 {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In this geometry (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>), the strength of the coupling is controlled by the distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between the loop and the radiating body, as well as by the shape factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(a,b)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">(a,b)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the loop. A rectangular sample of CNT buckypaper (of size <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D\times L</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">D\times L</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is thus placed in the space between the loop and the radiating dipole, this area being the most critical for the antenna's radiation performances.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>RFID tag: inductively coupled loop with a rectangular CNT load. The matching to the IC can be achieved for example by acting on the parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and by fixing the others.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The CNT film affects the coupling between the two structures, modifying the current's distribution, and consequently the input impedance of the tag. More specifically, the presence of the CNT film between the dipole and the loop produces a current flow between the two copper structures (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>), whose effect competes against the one produced by the inductive coupling: for extremely low conductivity, the prevailing effect is inductive, while, as well as the conductivity increases, the ohmic effect becomes stronger and the structure resembles, from a current point of view, a T-match feed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4">[28]</a>. Two different effects are hence present: ohmic currents that flow along <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a variation of the shape factor of the loop (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, center). As visible, the currents tend to reduce the length of the loop, flowing all along the surface and the perimeter of the CNT area. Both real and imaginary parts of the input impedance are accordingly dependent on the lossy CNT material.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Current distribution simulated by FDTD method. (<i>left</i>) Standard loop fed dipole (no CNT), (<i>center</i>) loop fed dipole integrating CNT, (<i>right</i>) conventional T-match dipole. Although the magnitude is quite similar, the currents are sensibly different in the CNT area, making the antenna very similar to the T-matched one.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>RFID radio-sensor integrating CNT equivalent circuit. A T-model has been adopted to represent the transformer in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4">[28]</a>. The parameters <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">R_{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">C_{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">L_{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (for clarity, grouped in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">Z_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) give the input impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">Z_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the radiating body near its (series) resonance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Circuit Model</h3><p>Under the hypothesis that the CNT can be considered as a lossy metal with variable conductivity, the input impedance of the radio sensor and its variation with the CNT conductivity can be described by the general equivalent circuit in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. The circuit has been obtained through a proper modification of the topology described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a">[28]</a> whose impedance transformer is replaced here by its T-model equivalent by introducing the series impedances <disp-formula id="" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{Z_{1}=&amp;\,j\omega L_{d}-Z_{T}\cr\noalign{{\hbox{and}}} Z_{2}=&amp;\,j\omega L_{l}-Z_{T}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-85">\eqalignno{Z_{1}=&amp;\,j\omega L_{d}-Z_{T}\cr\noalign{{\hbox{and}}} Z_{2}=&amp;\,j\omega L_{l}-Z_{T}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{Z_{1}=&amp;\,j\omega L_{d}-Z_{T}\cr\noalign{{\hbox{and}}} Z_{2}=&amp;\,j\omega L_{l}-Z_{T}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{T}=j\omega M\parallel Z_{\rm{CNT}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">Z_{T}=j\omega M\parallel Z_{\rm{CNT}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the modified impedance of transformation, which takes into account the presence of CNT <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(Z_{\rm{CNT}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">(Z_{\rm{CNT}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and of the mutual inductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> only related to the geometry of the structures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_4a">[30]</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">L_{l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the loop inductance, and finally <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{A}=R_{d}+1/j\omega C_{d}+j\omega L_{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">Z_{A}=R_{d}+1/j\omega C_{d}+j\omega L_{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> the input impedance of the radiating body around its first resonance. The presence of the CNT film impacts on the coupling between the dipole and the loop so that the input impedance at the chip port is finally given by <disp-formula id="deqn8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm in}=j\omega L_{l}+{{(Z_{T})^{2}}\over{Z_{A}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-91">Z_{\rm in}=j\omega L_{l}+{{(Z_{T})^{2}}\over{Z_{A}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">Z_{\rm in}=j\omega L_{l}+{{(Z_{T})^{2}}\over{Z_{A}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm{CNT}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">Z_{\rm{CNT}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is related to various CNT's parameters, such as its size, its conductivity, and the consequent skin effect <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\delta_{s}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">\delta_{s}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is roughly proportional to the surface impedance of imperfect conductors <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_4a">[31]</a> and can be evaluated by means of best fitting of the numerically computed input impedance to the circuital expression in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8" href="#deqn8" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a> in order to take into account the specific shape factor of the film. For the particular structure described in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>, <disp-formula id="" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm{CNT}}=f(\sigma,{\hbox{shape factor}}_{\rm{CNT}})\thickapprox K_{1}{{(1+j)}\over{\sigma\delta_{s}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-94">Z_{\rm{CNT}}=f(\sigma,{\hbox{shape factor}}_{\rm{CNT}})\thickapprox K_{1}{{(1+j)}\over{\sigma\delta_{s}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">Z_{\rm{CNT}}=f(\sigma,{\hbox{shape factor}}_{\rm{CNT}})\thickapprox K_{1}{{(1+j)}\over{\sigma\delta_{s}}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\delta_{s}=\sqrt{2/(\omega\mu_{r}\sigma)}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">\delta_{s}=\sqrt{2/(\omega\mu_{r}\sigma)}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the skin depth, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{r}=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">\mu_{r}=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the relative magnetic permeability of conductor and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> its conductivity. The loop inductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">L_{l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is mainly related to the geometric features of the structures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_4a">[30]</a>; however, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> (center), the presence on the CNT film in the inner part of the loop strongly modifies its current distribution, essentially reducing the overall perimeter of the effective current loop. The width of the horizontal segment <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w^{\prime\prime}(\sigma)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">w^{\prime\prime}(\sigma)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>) can thus be properly corrected to include this effect as <disp-formula id="" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w^{\prime\prime}\thickapprox w^{\prime}+(K_{2}\sigma+K_{3})\cdot a</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-100">w^{\prime\prime}\thickapprox w^{\prime}+(K_{2}\sigma+K_{3})\cdot a</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">w^{\prime\prime}\thickapprox w^{\prime}+(K_{2}\sigma+K_{3})\cdot a</span></span></disp-formula> with weights <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K_{2,3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">K_{2,3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to be defined through linear fitting.</p><p>It is worth noticing that for extremely low conductivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\sigma\rightarrow 0)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">(\sigma\rightarrow 0)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the CNT impedance becomes an open circuit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(Z_{\rm{CNT}}\rightarrow\infty)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">(Z_{\rm{CNT}}\rightarrow\infty)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{T}\rightarrow M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">Z_{T}\rightarrow M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as for the standard inductively coupled structure, while for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma\rightarrow\infty</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">\sigma\rightarrow\infty</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm{CNT}}\rightarrow 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">Z_{\rm{CNT}}\rightarrow 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{T}\rightarrow 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-107">Z_{T}\rightarrow 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (ohmic contact), giving rise to a T-match feed.</p><p>The circuit model in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> is of general application and could be used to support the design of other gas sensors integrating CNT with different conductivity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as well as to understand how this last parameter affects the tag's radiation performances. It is, however, worth noticing that since the circuit represents a hybrid between the T-match and the inductively coupled loop, it is reasonably valid only for relative low values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-109">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>: as the conductivity increases, a more suitable equivalent circuit model should be used to describe the T-match like structure <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a">[28]</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Parametric Analysis</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a> shows an example of parametric analysis, computed by the equivalent circuit model, for the loop-driven dipole in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> loaded by a 30 mm×10 mm CNT buckypaper with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma=2.5 {\hbox{S}}/{\hbox{m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">\sigma=2.5 {\hbox{S}}/{\hbox{m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as evaluated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, when varying the shape factor of the loop <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and its distance from the dipole <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Such analysis has been compared with the one produced by the full-wave FDTD simulation. For the particular geometry of the CNT, the following weights have been found by linear fitting <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K_{1}=1.7</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">K_{1}=1.7</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K_{2}=6\cdot 10^{-2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">K_{2}=6\cdot 10^{-2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K_{3}=-4\cdot 10^{-2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">K_{3}=-4\cdot 10^{-2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Parametric analysis of the input impedance varying the shape factor of the loop and its distance from the vertical dipole, having fixed (size in millimeters) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l=160</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">l=160</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w=5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">w=5</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L=30</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">L=30</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w^{\prime}=2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">w^{\prime}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b=22</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">b=22</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D=10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">D=10</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The input reactance is nearly unaffected by the loop-dipole distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For a fixed loop size, instead, the resistance reduces when the loop-dipole distance increases. For the particular choice of parameters as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a=10 {\hbox {mm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-123">a=10 {\hbox {mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d=2 {\hbox {mm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-124">d=2 {\hbox {mm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the predicted antenna impedance is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm in}(a,d)=17+j140 [\Omega]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">Z_{\rm in}(a,d)=17+j140 [\Omega]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, very close to the required value to match the NXP IC.</p><p>For this size of the loop, the variation of the input impedance at 915 MHz with conductivity is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma=[{1,5}] {\hbox{S}}/{\hbox{m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">\sigma=[{1,5}] {\hbox{S}}/{\hbox{m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Change of the input impedance of the loaded RFID tag with conductivity.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As expected from physical considerations, the variation of CNT conductivity impacts both the real and imaginary parts of the input impedance. They monotonically decrease as the conductivity increases according to different variation profiles. In percentage terms, the effect is stronger on the input resistance since the reactance is mainly governed by the shape factor of the loop, as indicated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. Moreover, the presence of the CNT will modify the losses of the tag, also producing a variation of gain.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Prototype</h3><p>A first prototype of the tag is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>. Voyantic Tagformance is used for the characterization of the RFID response of the tag. The interrogator antenna is a Kushcraft patch having a 6-dBi gain and a circular polarization. The reader's antenna-tag distance is fixed to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r=63.5 {\hbox {cm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-127">r=63.5 {\hbox {cm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Both the reader and the tag are 101 cm high from the floor. All the measurements have been performed in an anechoic chamber.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Photograph of prototype. Size in millimeters: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A=180</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" class="MathJax_Preview">B=80</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-129-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-129">B=80</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l=160</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-130-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-130">l=160</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w=5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-131-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-131">w=5</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L=30</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-132-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-132">L=30</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w^{\prime}=2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">w^{\prime}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a=10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-134">a=10</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b=22</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-135">b=22</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D=10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-136">D=10</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d=2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-137">d=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Simulation and measurement results for AID and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-138">G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the CNT-loaded RFID prototype.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The measured AID <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> and realized gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a>, as defined in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>, are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a> for three different orientations. The AID is independent of the reader-tag mutual position <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_4c">[26]</a>, while the realized gain is rather sensitive to the reader-tag orientation due to the variable gain of the tag over the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane. Simulation and measurements have been compared along the normal direction, e.g., when the tag is placed exactly in front of the reader. Although there are some deviations at the lower and higher frequencies, basically due to the nonlinearity of the IC, they reasonably fit around the designed frequency 915 MHz, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Measurement setup comprising the remotely controlled reader, the ammonia tank connected to the gas chamber, and the RFID TUT. The reader's antenna-tag distance is fixed to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r=63.5 {\hbox {cm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">r=63.5 {\hbox {cm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Turn-on power of the CNT loaded RFID tag with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-142">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Exposure and Recovery Measurement Time-Steps<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
It is important to point out the effect of the CNT buckypaper on the radiation performances of the tag. The maximum measured realized gain is around <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{-}{\hbox {7 dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-143-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-143">{-}{\hbox {7 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which implies a simulation gain of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{-}{\hbox {6 dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-144-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-144">{-}{\hbox {6 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, worse than typical gain for this kind of antenna (0–2 dB) due to the presence of a lossy loading.<p></p><p>The maximum reading distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r_{\rm Max}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-145-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-145">r_{\rm Max}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be evaluated from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1-2" href="#deqn1-2" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> enforcing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{R\rightarrow T}=P_{\rm{chip}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">P_{R\rightarrow T}=P_{\rm{chip}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Taking into account the measurement results and considering a reader emitting up to 4-W effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) in linear polarization, the estimated maximum read distance is 4 m.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Sensing Characterization</h2></div><p>To test the sensing performances of the tag, it has been placed into a 684-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox {cm}}^{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-147">{\hbox {cm}}^{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> plastic gas chamber, and a volume of 6 mL of 10% ammonia hydroxide was guided into it (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>). The reference condition for the tag, without ammonia, accounts for the presence of the gas chamber in close proximity of the radiating structures.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> shows the results of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P^{\rm to}[\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">P^{\rm to}[\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the tag-under-test (TUT) following the exposure to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-149">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The measurement time-steps are indicated in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. An immediate and sharp variation of response is observed at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t_{1}=1 {\hbox{min}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-150">t_{1}=1 {\hbox{min}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> followed by a saturation. Within the band of interest, the behavior is monotonic, with about 2 dB of overall variation. Since the turn-on power is inversely proportional to the realized gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}=G_{T}\cdot\tau</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-151-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-151">G_{\tau}=G_{T}\cdot\tau</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the tag, the diagrams in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> suggest that the tag performances improve along with the exposure to ammonia. This behavior seems to be in contrast with the two CNT-monopoles experiment in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, wherein <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert S12\vert^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-152-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-152">\vert S12\vert^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reduces as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">[{\hbox{HN}}_{3}]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-153-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-153">[{\hbox{HN}}_{3}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases. A possible explanation is that the presence of ammonia tends to improve the impedance matching <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\tau)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-154-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-154">(\tau)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between the tag and the microchip. A more detailed chemical analysis of the absorption should be nevertheless required to fully understand this effect.</p><p>It is worth noticing that the time required to take a complete measurement of data (840–980 MHz) is approximately 90 s, and thus it may be comparable with the response time of the sensor (approximately 2 min according to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5">[15]</a>). This could affect the accuracy of the data especially at higher frequencies since the absorbtion of the ammonia, and thus the electromagnetic features of the CNT, are changing in the meanwhile the measurement is performed. However, for the two UHF RFID frequencies considered in this paper (European and American bands), the measurement time can be assumed to be less than 40 s, and hence, the measurement artifact could be considered negligible.</p><p>The visible variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}[\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-155-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-155">G_{\tau}[\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-156-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-156">{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the presence of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-157-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-157">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a>) confirms that both input impedance and gain are affected by the gas. As expected, the latter indicator is more sensitive to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-158-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-158">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> than AID due to the additional dependence on the tag's gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{T}[\theta,\phi,\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-159-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-159">G_{T}[\theta,\phi,\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-160-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-160">G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and AID for the CNT-loaded RFID prototype with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-161-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-161">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>It is useful to introduce the percentage variation of realized gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-162-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-162">\Delta G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and AID <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm AID}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-163-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-163">\Delta {\rm AID}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> referred to the initial state <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-164-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-164">t_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> such as without ammonia in the air <disp-formula id="" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\xi (t_{i})={{\xi (t_{i})-\xi (t_{0})}\over{\xi (t_{0})}}\cdot 100</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-165-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-165">\Delta\xi (t_{i})={{\xi (t_{i})-\xi (t_{0})}\over{\xi (t_{0})}}\cdot 100</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\Delta\xi (t_{i})={{\xi (t_{i})-\xi (t_{0})}\over{\xi (t_{0})}}\cdot 100</span></span></disp-formula> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\xi=\{G_{\tau},{\rm{AID}}\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-166-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-166">\xi=\{G_{\tau},{\rm{AID}}\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17. </b><fig><p>Turn-on power of the CNT loaded RFID tag—recovery.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 18. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-167-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-167">G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and AID for the CNT-loaded RFID prototype with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-168-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-168">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>—recovery.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The maximum variation for both indicators arises just after the ammonia introduction, more specifically, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta G{}_{\tau}(t_{1})=30\%</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-169-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-169">\Delta G{}_{\tau}(t_{1})=30\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm{AID}}(t_{1})=10\%</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-170-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-170">\Delta {\rm{AID}}(t_{1})=10\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The total variation is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta G{}_{\tau}(t_{5})=60\%</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-171-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-171">\Delta G{}_{\tau}(t_{5})=60\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm{AID}}(t_{5})=20\%</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-172-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-172">\Delta {\rm{AID}}(t_{5})=20\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and seems to be maximum at 915 MHz.<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Recovery Features</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 17</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">18</a> show the recovery plots of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P^{\rm to}[\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-173-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-173">P^{\rm to}[\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}[\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-174-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-174">G_{\tau}[\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-175-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-175">{\rm{AID}}[\Psi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency after having removed the ammonia. A monotonic recovery characteristic is present with a slower response (see <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> for all the recovery time steps), mainly occurring in the first 15 min.</p><p>Although <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-176-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-176">G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> shows clear recovery features, the AID seems quite insensitive to the phenomena, especially at 870 MHz. This issue could be related to the fact that the dependence of the latter indicator only on the input impedance of the tag makes it less sensitive to the physical variation of the antenna.</p><p>When considering the whole cycle, it is apparent that the presence of ammonia irreversibly modifies the tag's radiation performances, producing an hysteresis in both input impedance and gain (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a>). A difference of about 10% in the turn-on power is indeed observed between the initial condition (without ammonia) and the final condition (after recovery).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6041062/6003806/6003806-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 19. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-177-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-177">G_{\tau}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and AID at 915 MHz during the exposure and the recovery process.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6003806/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Discussion and Conclusions</h2></div><p>The complete integration of CNT film into an RFID tag has been here reported for the first time aiming at designing and testing a fully working passive gas radio sensor. Simplified fabrication procedures, as well as indirect RF characterizations for the CNT buckypaper, have been proposed with promising results in term of feasibility and accuracy. The proof of concept of using a CNT-antenna and CNT-based passive RFID tag as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-178-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-178">{\hbox{NH}}_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> wireless sensors has been theoretically and experimentally verified in spite of the strikingly low <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-179-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-179">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the tested samples.</p><p>Beside the promising early results, the optimization of this class of chemical-doped RFID tags is still prone to considerable improvements concerning the technology process to produce the CNT buckypaper load, the antenna design, and not least, the interrogation algorithm.</p><p>The proposed fabrication procedure seems indeed to offer great opportunities in term of cost and simplicity, but it should be better controlled and optimized in order to get defect-free and reproducible sensitive films at the cost of the lowest CNT amount. Depending on the preparation technique and process, in fact, the properties and the behavior of the sensors can vary significantly, and this is a very crucial issue for the large-scale production of CNTs-based devices. Furthermore, in order to design efficient sensing systems, it is necessary to quantify, and especially to enhance, the gas sensitivity of the buckypaper, as well as its response time and selectivity. A functionalized CNT should be considered for this purpose. Possible improvements of the proposed evaporation technique can be achieved by producing a smaller area of buckypaper in order to better control the uniformity of the deposition and reduce the required amount of nanotubes. The long recovery time, which could be a limiting issue for real-time monitoring of oscillating events, could instead find interesting application for a one-shot sensor, e.g., by taking advantage of the permanent physical modifications especially visible in the AID response.</p><p>In order to fully control the tag's behavior in time-varying boundary conditions, the electromagnetic design of the radio sensor needs further refinements, for instance, by employing multiphysics models. Recent studies <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_6">[4]</a> demonstrate the possibility to control and enhance the sensitivity and the dynamic range of a passive RFID sensor just in the design phase by properly choosing the IC family and the process's realization, thus forcing the antenna to have the best impedance matching to the RFID IC.</p><p>Finally, the interrogation of the tag in real-world environments could present big challenges, especially concerning the natural fluctuation of the electromagnetic responses caused by the multipath. If the measurement is performed in static conditions, e.g., the mutual position between the reader and the sensor tag remains unchanged during the whole phenomenon to monitor, or similarly, a same measurement setup can be exactly replicated in successive readings, the turn-on indicator gives a feasible and sharp response. More in general, the AID metric could be a solution to reduce the reading uncertainties, but further effort is required to better enhance its dynamic range in a controlled way.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank the Georgia Tech Nanotechnology Research Center, Atlanta, for offering help in the fabrication processes.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
